## Section 001: Rust Legacy Coder Prompts
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names a theme but does not explain whether these prompts are executable instructions, historical evidence, a migration aid, or current Rust doctrine
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because legacy prompts bundle durable first principles with local rituals, dated crate examples, unsupported numbers, duplicated catalogs, and broad commands, so safe reuse requires classification before instruction
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a whole prompt is pasted into context as authority, four-word naming becomes a language law, cargo clean becomes routine, editorial scores become measured confidence, or current API behavior is inferred from unbrowsed links
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for prompt interpretation and migration; it does not replace current compiler, crate, framework, repository, security, or product evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a source-generation model, reuse protocol, rejection criteria, verification ladder, and no-browse boundary before preserving the seed mappings
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the value of a legacy prompt is not obedience to its wording but the recoverable decision history showing which rules survived critique and which became explicit boundaries
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat this reference as a provenance-aware migration and critique guide: recover intent from rust-coder-01, use rust-coder-02 to identify reliability gaps and general-versus-local distinctions, and use Rust-Coder-1000IQ-01 as the more rigorous operator doctrine subject to repository and task verification

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for prompt interpretation and migration; it does not replace current compiler, crate, framework, repository, security, or product evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Legacy Coder Prompts", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a source-generation model, reuse protocol, rejection criteria, verification ladder, and no-browse boundary before preserving the seed mappings

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists three local files and four public links but assigns every local file the same artifact role, omits byte identity and generation order, and marks public sources as facts without recording whether they were actually opened
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because generation, purpose, and retrieval status determine whether a sentence is historical intent, comparative critique, operational doctrine, or an unverified ecosystem pointer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: file count substitutes for corroboration, a later document is automatically treated as correct, a declared normative status overrides repository rules, or a URL row implies current framework behavior without a complete read
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the map establishes provenance and reuse pressure, not universal technical truth or present ecosystem compatibility
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to enrich the mapping with generation, hash, authority basis, limitation, dependency, retrieval status, conflict, and promotion-gate columns while retaining every seed row
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that three files are not three votes; they form an evolution chain whose disagreements reveal where prompt rules needed boundaries, evidence, or replacement

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists context-free summaries, unsourced claims, and unverified instructions, but it omits the legacy-specific hazards exposed by duplicated prompts, local rituals, editorial scores, stale APIs, catalog overload, and universal command or performance claims
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because legacy prompt failures usually occur when context or normative strength is silently widened, so detection must identify the exact transfer that made a once-useful instruction unsafe
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the registry mocks obviously bad code, safer replacement is another slogan, a smell is prohibited without an exception boundary, or detection depends on the same source that introduced the claim
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry blocks unsafe prompt reuse but does not replace code review, threat analysis, semver evaluation, or runtime diagnosis
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three generic rows into a source-aware causal registry with widening mechanism, exception, containment, replacement, proof, and ownership
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a legacy anti-pattern is often a scope mutation rather than a technically false sentence; preserving the original boundary can recover the value

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the archive verifier passes while this packet is malformed, a generic Cargo command is run from the wrong root, an unsupported tool is declared mandatory, a prior result is reused, or compilation is reported as proof of cancellation or semver safety

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says to open this reference on a theme or path match and then load local sources, prefer gated patterns, check public freshness, and preserve labels, but it does not classify user intent, task mode, risk surface, or legacy migration depth
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the same legacy sentence can be useful evidence in a history audit, harmful as an implementation command, or appropriate as a local convention, depending on mode and authority
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a keyword selects the whole prompt, mode remains implicit, review output turns into implementation, historical facts become recommendations, or the agent loads broad catalogs before inspecting the actual code and requirements
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the guide to decide how to reason and retrieve; it does not authorize edits, destructive actions, external research, or completion claims beyond the user's scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace keyword-only triggering with intent and mode classification, risk and boundary inventory, progressive retrieval, output contract, verification, and stop rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that prompt routing is a control-flow decision: choosing mode first prevents context retrieval from predetermining the answer

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed offers Adopt, Adapt, Avoid, and Cost of being wrong, but it compares only local-versus-external agreement and does not distinguish verbatim preservation, causal adaptation, replacement, specialist routing, or retirement
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because two instructions can both sound idiomatic while imposing different obligations; explicit tradeoffs reveal when compatibility, ownership simplicity, diagnosability, or bounded shutdown outweighs stylistic consistency
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: Adopt means sources agree without code evidence, Adapt changes wording but not scope, Avoid discards a useful local rule, or Cost of wrong mentions only wasted time while ignoring public API and runtime damage
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this guide structures a technical decision and cannot decide product value, legal policy, threat acceptance, or organizational ownership without stakeholders
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand the four rows into six disposition choices with causal criteria, caller and lifecycle costs, evidence, rollback, and revisit conditions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the key tradeoff is not old versus new; it is which rule places the unavoidable complexity at the boundary best equipped to own and verify it

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed calls rust-coder-01 canonical, rust-coder-02 legacy historical, and 1000IQ supporting, but complete reads show a chronological and functional hierarchy in which rust-coder-02 explicitly succeeds and critiques the first file while 1000IQ is the most operationally rigorous working draft
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because one global canonical label cannot describe a corpus where different documents own provenance, correction, and execution semantics
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: newest automatically wins, oldest remains canonical by seed label, document length becomes authority, a working draft's MUST overrides codebase policy, or multiple sources repeat one unsupported claim and inflate confidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy orders these local prompt artifacts only and cannot supersede compiler guarantees, current dependency contracts, repository tests, or user requirements
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the single canonical/supporting/legacy ranking with a claim-specific provenance, critique, operational, and local-override hierarchy while retaining the seed classification as historical metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that authority is multidimensional: historical authenticity, explanatory critique, and operational completeness can belong to different files simultaneously
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to use a faceted hierarchy: rust-coder-01 is the historical baseline and origin for local rituals, rust-coder-02 is the reliability curation and critique bridge, 1000IQ is the operational working doctrine, and explicit repository rules outrank all three for local behavior

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; newest automatically wins, oldest remains canonical by seed label, document length becomes authority, a working draft's MUST overrides codebase policy, or multiple sources repeat one unsupported claim and inflate confidence

- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the single canonical/supporting/legacy ranking with a claim-specific provenance, critique, operational, and local-override hierarchy while retaining the seed classification as historical metadata

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the bad case is absurd, the good case assumes a greenfield codebase, examples vary only in wording, tests are omitted, or the borderline case becomes an unreviewed permanent exception

- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace source-loading contrasts with concrete trait, naming, cleaning, error, and compatibility migrations that include consequences, tests, alternatives, and limits

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed tracks compile attempts and review comments and watches hidden ownership or error tradeoffs, but these workflow counts neither isolate prompt quality nor detect stale rules, over-abstraction, compatibility damage, cancellation failures, unsupported claims, or expired waivers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a fast compile loop can coexist with the wrong contract, while a slower migration that prevents public or lifecycle damage may be the better outcome
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: fewer comments mean quality, more traits mean testability, all Clippy warnings mean correctness, one migration supplies percentages, agents self-score their own routing, or teams suppress disagreement to improve a dashboard
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: measure prompt migration and technical decision quality, not individual productivity, causal business impact, or production reliability without separate evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to demote compile and comment counts to secondary context and add source, routing, contract, failure, compatibility, verification, waiver, and disagreement feedback loops
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the best feedback signal is fewer boundary surprises: generated guidance should predict what callers, tasks, errors, and gates actually do

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks seven document features but does not prove complete source reads, generation-aware hierarchy, local-versus-general classification, legacy-rule disposition, mode fit, caller and lifecycle analysis, normalized packet uniqueness, frozen-span preservation, or fresh task-specific evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a document can look complete while still smuggling one unsupported legacy instruction into active guidance or placing correct packet answers under the wrong section
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: heading presence proves coverage, source paths prove full reads, unique wrapper prefixes prove substantive uniqueness, compilation proves behavior, or no open question is mistaken for no uncertainty
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the artifact gate to this file and the migration gate to consequential rule reuse; scale ceremony down explicitly only when risk is genuinely local and reversible

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because specialized references own current operational evidence that a historical prompt atlas cannot safely reconstruct, while this file preserves the source and disposition record they need
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing follows a keyword, several destinations are listed without selection, the target is assumed current from its filename, historical rationale is discarded, or two agents edit the same artifact
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not route away merely because another file mentions Rust; hand off only when a narrower current obligation governs the next decision
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace three generic adjacent labels with trigger-to-path routes, precedence, handoff payload, co-ownership prohibition, completion, and return checks

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within do not route away merely because another file mentions Rust; hand off only when a narrower current obligation governs the next decision
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: replace three generic adjacent labels with trigger-to-path routes, precedence, handoff payload, co-ownership prohibition, completion, and return checks

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed frames systems, CLI, service, async, and safety-sensitive use, then imposes one crate, 100 changed symbols, and one integration path without evidence; it also truncates the rust-coder-01 heading list and ignores source-generation and rule-migration complexity
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because migration effort grows with independent obligations and consumers, not with a fixed symbol count; one sentence can alter a public API or shutdown protocol across many call sites
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a small text edit changes broad generated behavior, a large private wording cleanup is split by symbol count, one record mixes unrelated modes, or source discovery expands without a stop rule
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this workload model governs prompt evolution and associated code decisions; production capacity and organizational planning require separate evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace fixed symbol capacity and truncated heading pressure with rule, source, mode, contract, risk, verification, split, ownership, and rollback dimensions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the unit of prompt migration is a coherent instruction contract whose provenance, downstream effect, and rollback can be verified together

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets complete evidence labels, 18-of-20 decision accuracy, zero unsupported operational claims, and recovery clarity, but the sampled threshold lacks a baseline and the targets omit source-generation accuracy, rule disposition, repository override, waiver expiry, packet grouping, and downstream contract outcomes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because structural consistency cannot prevent an agent from faithfully applying the wrong generation or scope, while a fixed small-sample percentage creates certainty without statistical support
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: selected easy cases produce accuracy, deterministic checks are averaged with judgments, agents grade their own migrations, one root error counts as many independent failures, or no corrective action follows a breach
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: these targets assess prompt migration and reference use; service availability, security, and product correctness require specialized objectives
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain auditable evidence and unsupported-claim invariants, remove the fixed 18-of-20 threshold, and add source, mode, disposition, compatibility, lifecycle, waiver, and grouping targets
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability is the chance that a migrated instruction preserves the intended contract under a real repository and failure path, not the consistency of its prose

### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that reliability is the chance that a migrated instruction preserves the intended contract under a real repository and failure path, not the consistency of its prose
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from structural consistency cannot prevent an agent from faithfully applying the wrong generation or scope, while a fixed small-sample percentage creates certainty without statistical support
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where selected easy cases produce accuracy, deterministic checks are averaged with judgments, agents grade their own migrations, one root error counts as many independent failures, or no corrective action follows a breach

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: enumerate all high-risk decisions, use double review for ambiguous dispositions, audit regressions and waivers, maintain qualitative case studies at low volume, or defer numeric targets until a stable baseline exists This changes how the section resolves which measurable properties make repeated legacy-prompt migration trustworthy rather than merely uniform.

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table

- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed includes source drift, generic advice, runtime contention, and production panic, but it omits authority inversion, local-rule universalization, stale example copying, rule-buffet overdesign, public compatibility breakage, unowned task migration, waiver rot, false completion, and malformed packet ownership

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed limits stale-evidence refresh, stops work on red gates, checkpoints long workflows, and assigns one owner, but it does not distinguish prompt regeneration, source retrieval, flaky verification, deterministic code failure, or production retry semantics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retry consumes context, time, compute, and often external capacity; repeating without a new information path can reinforce prompt bias, hide tests that fail consistently, duplicate effects, or delay shutdown
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the agent re-prompts until a preferred answer appears, reruns Cargo until green, reloads every large source after each question, retries a public write without deduplication, or treats contradictory sources as transient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs reference work and generic lifecycle hygiene; application network, storage, queue, and payment retries require protocol-specific evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate source reread, public refresh, prompt regeneration, test replay, deterministic repair, and runtime retry, with budgets, new-evidence criteria, idempotency, stop conditions, and routes
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure protects epistemic quality as well as resources: stopping prevents repeated outputs from becoming false corroboration
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify first: reread an incomplete local span deterministically, refresh stale public evidence once when authorized, replay a suspected flaky observation under a bounded diagnostic plan, fix deterministic failures, and route production retries to a domain reference that can prove idempotency, deadlines, capacity, and cancellation

- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: this evidence is appropriate because the seed supports bounded evidence refresh and workflow backpressure, while the local successors explicitly address retries, bounded queues, cancellation, completion honesty, and checkpoint discipline
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verification cannot erase the judgment that the corpus defines no universal prompt, time, token, attempt, queue, or service budget
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: reject evidence gathered outside this boundary: this section governs reference work and generic lifecycle hygiene; application network, storage, queue, and payment retries require protocol-specific evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: add pass/fail observations tied to the revision separate source reread, public refresh, prompt regeneration, test replay, deterministic repair, and runtime retry, with budgets, new-evidence criteria, idempotency, stop conditions, and routes

### Question 09: What is known confidently, and what remains judgment or uncertainty?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the confident evidence is the seed supports bounded evidence refresh and workflow backpressure, while the local successors explicitly address retries, bounded queues, cancellation, completion honesty, and checkpoint discipline

### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that backpressure protects epistemic quality as well as resources: stopping prevents repeated outputs from becoming false corroboration
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from retry consumes context, time, compute, and often external capacity; repeating without a new information path can reinforce prompt bias, hide tests that fail consistently, duplicate effects, or delay shutdown
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where the agent re-prompts until a preferred answer appears, reruns Cargo until green, reloads every large source after each question, retries a public write without deduplication, or treats contradictory sources as transient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within this section governs reference work and generic lifecycle hygiene; application network, storage, queue, and payment retries require protocol-specific evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: separate source reread, public refresh, prompt regeneration, test replay, deterministic repair, and runtime retry, with budgets, new-evidence criteria, idempotency, stop conditions, and routes
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: narrow the query, inspect the exact span, stop generation, quarantine a flaky test, fix the deterministic cause, pause producers, shed optional work, preserve a dead-letter record, roll back, or request human adjudication This changes how the section resolves when another prompt, source read, test run, or runtime attempt can add evidence and what backpressure prevents repeated work from laundering a contradiction or overloading the system.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, proof commands, latency percentiles, errors, timeouts, retries, saturation, rollback, and compact audit evidence, but it does not expose source generation, mode, rule disposition, repository override, waiver, generated-output effect, or downstream Rust lifecycle correlation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because observability should connect a migrated instruction to an observable decision and behavior; raw transcripts and aggregate metrics cannot show which scope assumption failed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: hidden reasoning or full prompts are logged, secrets or code payloads escape, free-form summaries cannot be queried, editorial scores become telemetry, average latency lacks workload, or runtime events cannot trace back to a migrated rule
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist governs decision and technical evidence records, not legal discovery, privacy compliance, production SLO design, or chain-of-thought capture
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the generic signals into a redacted source-to-disposition-to-code observation schema with stable fields, lifecycle correlation, access, retention, and response ownership
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that migration observability should capture explicit decision rationale and evidence, not private thought process; this keeps audits useful without turning context into a liability

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed demands memory, panic, concurrency evidence and a universal local p95 below 10 ms, then mixes runtime latency with compile attempts, tool calls, source count, and reviewer decision time without a causal model
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because legacy sources contain precise timing and productivity assertions without supporting datasets, while build cache, context size, allocator, hardware, runtime topology, and input distribution can dominate observed results
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the 10 ms threshold is reused universally, compile attempts imply development speed, fewer tokens imply better decisions, debug builds support release claims, averages hide tails, or optimization weakens cancellation, API clarity, or proof without requirement value
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: measurements support only the declared operation and environment; production capacity, cost, and team productivity need broader evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to remove the universal p95 gate and unsupported speed implications, split workflow and runtime methods, and add reproducibility, correctness, variance, adverse-case, decision, and rollback controls
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance evidence is valuable when it can veto a legacy optimization or workflow ritual that adds complexity without moving the actual constraint

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, more than one ownership boundary, unbounded discovery, production traffic without an SLO, distributed file edits, context drift, and an unnarrowed large codebase, but one ownership transfer is too low a cutoff and prompt-scale risks are absent
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because scale becomes unsafe when no reviewer can reconstruct how a rule propagates or reverse it coherently, not merely when code crosses more than one ordinary ownership boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one packet hides independent migrations, agents edit the same file, a split loses shared source decisions, downstream outputs are sampled without rationale, production changes proceed without specialized objectives, or line count alone triggers decomposition
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference may remain provenance input after routing but cannot own fleet rollout, organization-wide governance, live service migration, or threat acceptance
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the one-ownership cutoff with prompt-propagation and evidence-closure criteria, explicit decomposition axes, one-writer ownership, integration, rollback, and re-entry checks
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the scale limit is traceability closure: a migration is too large when rule lineage, consequence, and recovery cannot be reviewed as one coherent unit
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to continue while one owner can connect every migrated instruction to provenance, affected outputs, contracts, tests, and rollback; split or route when independent repositories, prompt families, public APIs, runtime domains, unsafe proofs, security boundaries, live migrations, unbounded source discovery, or parallel writers defeat that closure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because scale becomes unsafe when no reviewer can reconstruct how a rule propagates or reverse it coherently, not merely when code crosses more than one ordinary ownership boundary

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference may remain provenance input after routing but cannot own fleet rollout, organization-wide governance, live service migration, or threat acceptance
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the one-ownership cutoff with prompt-propagation and evidence-closure criteria, explicit decomposition axes, one-writer ownership, integration, rollback, and re-entry checks

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined-inference labels but omits claim locators, source hashes, generation relationships, missing upstream dependencies, external retrieval status, editorial-score treatment, conflict rules, confidence updates, and refresh triggers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a local file can be directly observed yet still be historically stale or normatively weak, while a preserved public URL supplies no present factual support until read
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: three distinct files are counted as agreement without comparing lineage, a URL is called current, missing Notes2026 inputs are silently treated as read, the seed's canonical label becomes technical truth, or hashes are mistaken for correctness
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the ledger provides artifact traceability, not authorship proof, legal provenance, upstream endorsement, security assurance, or current ecosystem certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three labels into claim-level hash, generation, status, read state, dependency, conflict, inference, evidence grade, verification, and refresh rules with explicit no-browse and missing-source notes
